Since I was eating by myself I only got the Champa sampler plate which gives you threedifferent appetizer items. It was actually too much food just for myself. <Text>My roommate took yesterday for the first time and I thoroughly enjoyed the food! We went at 6pm because he said it gets very busy, and I'm so glad we did. It's a small-ish place with majority of the tables that sit 4 people. It has a nice atmosphere and the staff seem very nice.

<userid>113339104060067052308< /userid><name>Vic</name>< time>
1385063064598</time>
< Rating>
3< /Rating>
< text>
My girlfriend, friends, and I have been frequenting the original Oakland location for nearly half a decade, so we were excited to learn that they had a new location in SF, where we live. For the record, I have rated the Oakland location with 5 stars and have recommended it to many people. Unfortunately, this location does not satisfy and live up to the Champa Garden name.

The original location has the best Pad Thai, hands down. I brought a group of friends who have never had Champa Garden to this location and enthusiastically recommended the Pad Thai; unfortunately, all of them stated it was the absolute worst Pad Thai they have ever had. The overpowering taste of ketchup was the only flavor in this dish. (By the way, authentic Pad Thai does not contain ketchup, but I am generally fine with ketchup in this dish because most American Thai restaurants cook it that way).

The basil fried rice was lacking, as well, which was disappointing because the Oakland location's version is one of my favorite fried rice dishes. Other dishes we tried were uninspired and did not warrant another order. The only saving grace is the rice ball salad, which my friends stated they would probably place pick-up orders for in the future. At least this popular appetizer is as good at this restaurant.

Additionally, the service was very poor. We had to ask for water refills a few times, and it took at least 10 minutes just to get each refill. Our appetizers came promptly, but there was at least a 15-minute wait between finishing our appetizers and the entrees' arrival.

I initially planned to rate this restaurant with 2 stars because it was disheartening to have this location be that much worse than the original. However, I took a step back and thought a 3-star rating would make more sense: it may not be anywhere close to the original restaurant, but it is still better than some Thai restaurants in SF and does not fully deserve a 2-star rating. I hope to return to this restaurant in the future; perhaps by then, they will have worked out all their kinks.</text>

<GmapID>0x808f7dcdc78686e7:0xd4c8b792d4203469< /GmapID><Rating>3<//Rating></record>

< Gmap_id>
0x808f7dcdc78686e7:0xd4c8b792d4203469<//Gmap_id>
< date>
1392924698668</date>
<Response>None< /Response><Pics>None</Pics><name>Tina Chan Ling< /name>< Review>
Champa Garden is a wonderful addition to the neighborhood! They serve Laotian cuisine and everything we ordered was uber tasty!

We ordered the Champa Sampler which included a rice ball salad, lao sausage made with lemongrass, and fried spring rolls. The rice ball salad was my favorite from the sampler because it had a little spicy kick to it; loved all the different ingredients such as mint, cilantro, and peanuts which helped provide a nice refreshing bite when everything was combined together.

Lue's Noodle Soup (Kaow Soy) listed that it had fermented bean in it, which didn't initially appeal to me but I'm glad we decided to give it a try! It came with wide rice noodles and minced pork and the fermented bean taste was really faint. It looks spicy but isn't - great flavors and the dish was large enough to share.

The Duck Curry is also worth ordering if you are craving curry. The sauce was not watery nor too milky and they are generous with their chunks of duck meat, eggplants, and peppers! Rice is not included but this is definitely one of the better curries I've had in a really long time.

Overall I'd recommend coming here if you are seeking some flavorful Southeast Asian food with great service! The waitresses were attentive and the food came out quick, I'll be back soon!< /Review>

<Text>Great casual dining place, delicious vegetarian options too!< /Text><Pictures>None</Pictures><Resp>None< /Resp><Gmap_id>0x808f7dcdc78686e7:0xd4c8b792d4203469<//Gmap_id></record></dataset><record>

116245069998444262666<//UserId.>
<name>Cheryl Young< /name><date>1405663334316<//date>< rating>
4</rating>
<review>As a fan of the Oakland location, I was excited to hear they expanded across the bay after I made my move back to the City.

I come here strictly for the Laotian specialties so I cannot comment on the Thai food. The rice ball salad is a delicious blend of crunchy fried rice, bits of tasty sausage, and fresh herbs. It is only second to Vientiane in Oakland. The Lao sausage is also a flavor bomb. And if you like your papaya salad funky and spicy, Champa's Lao version will not disappoint.

While many are a fan of Lue's noodle soup, I favor the soothing Lao version of chicken noodle soup, kao piak. This is made with thick (udon girth), fresh rice noodles that impart an excellent chew, and comes with a hefty amount of chicken and the right sprinkling of fried shallot and green onion.

I have seen waits to be seated here since the space is smallish and they don't jam too many tables in. However, they pack their to-go noodle soups well, by separating out the noodles from the broth and accompaniments. Service is fair and the space is noticeably clean and benefits in ambiance from the large windows facing the street.

Parking can be tight on Ocean, but can be found nearby on residential streets. All in all, I give an edge to their Oakland location for portions and consistency but that is almost entirely compensated for this location being on my current side of the Bay.< /review><pictures>None<//pictures>< Resp>
None</Resp>

<text>Wonderfully delectable chartucerie plates and oysters farmed by the owner, Sebastian.  The food and drinks are locally sourced!  The oysters are medium sized, not overly briny or have sediment in them as with other places.  We both loved them with the summer mignonette, which is reminiscent of a cool and refreshing summer drink.  We had the smoked salmon and the Cypress Grove cheese platters.  The Wycliff Brut paired well with the food.  The setting is in a beautifully restored building with reclaimed, varnished wood tables, subtle modern touches and outdoor seating available with heat lamps.  Sebastian was a wonderful host/server and very attentive.<//text><Pics>None< /Pics><Resp>None<//Resp>< gmap_id>

<rating>5</rating><Response>None<//Response>< Gmap_id>

<Time>1438714889754< /Time><UserId.>114472612135563617838</UserId.><Pictures>None<//Pictures>< Text>
Humboldt Bay Oyster Tour Terrific!

Humboldt Bay (and the Arcata Bay portion in particular) is home to some of the world's best oysters - and oyster farmers!  The Oyster Tour is a terrific way to learn about how oysters are grown - a surprisingly hands-on process.

I'd say we are in the early stages of what may be called "the craft oyster movement" (like the craft beer movement of the 1980's and 1990's).  Oyster farmers are experimenting with a range of variables to explore the resulting shapes, growth rates, and tastes.  It appears that location has a great deal of impact, for example, and oyster beds just a few hundred meters away from one another may yield surprisingly different oysters - this is now known as "merroir".

Sebastian is both the tour guide and one of these local farmers.  Full of facts and surprising anecdotes about oysters, oyster farming, clam farming (yes, the Bay producers millions of baby clams that are then raised elsewhere) and the Bay itself.

You'll see oysters that are just a few weeks old, to those ready to be harvested, to some approaching 30 cm in length (OK, a foot long) - and you'll choose a few to sample when you return ashore.

If you like oysters and have a desire to learn a bit more about them first-hand, this tour is highly recommended.

Bring waterproof boots (the higher the better), as you'll hop out of the boat at the farm to explore the beds.  Bring several layers of clothing - and sunscreen, depending on the weather.<//Text>

Peter Cohan< /username>

<Name>Dayton Pickering< /Name><time>1614874317389<//time>< Review>
Been wanting to try this place for awhile so I was excited it finally opened in oaktown. Went around 2pm on a Wednesday afternoon- when you would typically expect it to be pretty dead. We ordered two pizzas to try- the big von and the spicy ellen. After waiting over 45 minutes we have to complain- the person who took our order didn't say anything about a long wait and there was only one other person who ordered after us and 6 people working. Never expected it to take that long given all the circumstances, we would've gone somewhere else! Pizza was good, we expected the big von to be a little spicy because of the hot honey. It was just sweet, but good. The spicy ellen was definitely spicy! It needed the honey. DO NOT buy the ranch- it tastes like the garbage you get at domino's, and they only offer it in a three pack for $2.50. Overall it was good but we would much rather go to any of the other amazing pizza options in the area. It's very pricy and the wait is just too long.</Review>

Have been going here since this place has opened. Tonight we walked out! The reason being, that we were told that they will no longer make any of our regular sushi iteams and put limits on what can be ordered (how does that work for an all you can eat) this is the ONLY reason we go to the Sushi & Gogi Palace. Prior to being told this. A party of 6 (regulars) walked out due to change. Unfortunately, they just lost business of 2 different parties of (weekly) regulars within 20 minutes. Something is fishy with this restaurant every week we come in there is NEVER the same sushi chef. Customer services and good food is what keeps people coming back, they are lacking customer service and in my opinion the last 3-4 times we have eaten here the sushi quality have gone down hill. Hate to say it but we will not be returning to this restaurant. Very disappointing.</review>

<Review>Every year my family makes the trek from SoCal to vacation in Shaver Lake and every year I pass by the Chuck Wagon in Sager California wondering what magic resides in this walk-up food shack with the proclamation...Home of the "Chili Dog". This year my wife helped me with this bucket-list item by agreeing to stop at Chuck Wagon for lunch before heading into the Sierras. Was it a good "Chili Dog" you ask? Oh Yes, a very good chili dog...I would highly recommend it if you like Chili Dogs. But, if you do not like chili dogs this will not convert you.  The Chili Cheese Fries are also great, they put lettuce on top...I think that is the Chuck Wagon version of a salad. The star of the show is probably the Frito Pie my wife ordered. What is a Frito Pie you ask?...One small bag of Frito corn chips sliced open sideways, and then add chili, cheese, onions, and lettuce...served with a spork. Delicious!

I love that this place has existed for all these years and just keeps on going. It was obvious that it is popular with locals, not many tourists stopping in. Would I go back? You bet! That being said I don't think it will become a yearly tradition as my wife and daughter were not as thrilled with the Chuck Wagon as myself. But this place put a huge smile on my face and I will surely be back their again some day.</Review><UserId.>107912069581893217197</UserId.>< Response>

Elizabeth Steinhauer-Clark<//name>
<review>The Chuck Wagon is a Sanger, CA institution.  As a long, long, long time Sanger resident I may be biased, but I do love this place.  If you have never been there before, it may seem intimidating but the staff is willing to answer questions.  The "Clark Burger" (no affiliation) is your standard double cheeseburger.  The chili is a meat (no beans) chili.  If you like good, greasy chili, then you will like this.  Much better (IMHO) than Tommy's in Southern California.  I know from which I speak on that point, as I went to school in SoCal and spent many a late night at Tommy's.

Fries are crinkle cut and always done to perfection.   I recommend using them to scoop up any chili that has fallen off of or out of your chili dog or Chili Clark.

Best bets? Most anything with chili on it - chili dog, chili cheese fries, chili Clark.  Note that chili cheese fries come with lettuce and onions on them.  I order without those items, but it is a matter of personal preference.

I will forever (or until such time as they get a new shake machine) miss having a chocolate milkshake with my chili dog.<//review><Pictures>None< /Pictures><UserId.>117960634216369547783</UserId.></record></dataset><record>

< review>
Best chili cheese fries, hands down! You just walk up, place your order, wait to be called, get your food, and either walk around back to the picnic tables, or get to where you're gonna be real quick, so you can enjoy some awesomely bomb chili. My favorite item is the chili cheese dog. It's a foot long dog, covered in their chili & cheese. I get it with onions, but whatever. Lol Anyway, they have a cool menu, oh and delicious shakes as well! I HighLee recommend this local staple.</review>

< Review>
I've been living in Sanger for 20 Years and I must say this place is definitely a staple for this city. Throughout the years, prices have always remained constantly low. Now add the combination of Cheese and chili and you've got yourself a tasty and cost efficient meal.

If you're new to the place, great starter items are the Chili Cheese Fries and Chili Cheese dog.< /Review>

<UserId.>102217017799646325370</UserId.><username>Bruce M<//username>< Date>
1497197933445<//Date>
<rate>3< /rate>< Review>
I got a Clark burger plain (just meat and cheese on a bun), wife got a chilli cheese dog with onions, and we split chilli cheese fries without onions. The chilli is sauce and ground beef without beans. The fries are the crinkle cut type.
I thought the chilli has a light taste reminiscent of the taco meat that you get from Taco Bell but the wife disagreed.
Overall the taste of the food isn't going to explode in your mouth. It's plain. The burger was lightly seasoned and I'd say the taste in the meat was mostly from the grill rather than seasoning. I think the key here is to get the chilli sauce on your hot dog or hamburger.  Even if you do get the chilli it's not aggressive, it's not going to make you think it's homemade and it's not going to win any chilli contest. It's also not likely to give you heartburn which is a plus.
Lastly, the chilli cheese fries came out less warm than you would expect. This could be due to the wait time. We went on a Saturday at about 630PM and there was a sizeable line and we waited about 15 minutes to get our order.</Review>
